--- 帖子 #1482 ---
How to use kino T3MA Ribbon Filled in FX-50 Scalping System……

We are familiar with filtering zones, like that of MTF Has Bars and all kinds of other bars to determine influence of higher TF’s on trade setups. Thanks to Kinonen who developed the ribbon version of T3MA it’s now possible to have a different view on tradingzones versus non trading zones immediately in the chart itself.

About a year ago I came across a trading system using T3MA’s very intelligently (trendtrading http://www.forex-tsd.com/suggestions...e-mtf-has.html), developed by Radatats.
So for all the fundamentals on T3MA’s you have to go there…..

Using this system for quite while I noticed that if one would use two T3MA’s instead of one…. It’s easier to determine better trade setups, because now you could notice how price rises up out of the zone between them……… or falls out of this zone. Quite often you can see here the formation of triangles before price breaks out!

My reasoning regarding all of this is the simple conclusion that at each TF level there are traders that move fast and there are others that move slow. When price arrives at a high probability trade the majority of fast movers at each level tend to enter and exit a trade near the faster T3MA and the majority of slow movers tend to enter and exit trades near the slower T3MA of the ribbon…. The rest of the traders trade in chaos, using all kinds of different timing.
This results in higher grades of support and resistance right at the edges of the ribbons. Example: when you see price f.i. fall out the Green TF1 ribbon line and next it retraces towards this Green line and next being rejected this is most of the time the start of high probability trade. Example 3 shows the beginning of such a trade…. Three bouncing retracements in a row at a very narrow TF1 ribbon Green and Red line very Close = High resistance.

In fact in my FX-50 Scalping setup the fundamental go / no go of a trade is still also being determined by #Kino_CCI_RSI_v5…. So nothing new there, though I strongly advise to always check for divergencies as well…. Crossing of the Blue CCI and Gray CCI near the zero line are the better indications for starting a trade. A continued trade is usually possible when the Gray CCI stays on the same side of the zero line and the Blue CCI crosses again in the same direction….. or sharply rises or falls out of the Gray CCI in the same direction….

New in this setup is, that there are three T3MA ribbon zones visisble: a TF1 ribbon (darkest colours, edges red and green), a TF 5 Ribbon (less dark colours )  and a TF 15 ribbon (yet lesser dark colours). This is all calculated in a similar way as in the Rads System….. just by multiplication. The TF 15 zone has been adjusted a little for Volume Factor. Using higher TF zones is not useful for our Scalping purposes…. Therefore these are left aside.

Zone Characteristics:

1. When price rises from or falls out of all three zones at the same time (especially when they are very narrow and close together) it’s going to be a high probability trade. Price goes into black area. These are by far the best trade setups….. for the simple reason that there is no price rejection by one of the other ribbons !!!!  Look at example in chart 1.

2. When price rises from TF1 ribbon and TF1 ribbon starts rising above TF5 and TF15 ribbons (Strong Uptrend), it’s very likely that this breakout to the upside will present more than one trade. Most of the time two or three trades are possible here. The same goes for the opposite direction when price falls out of TF1 ribbon and TF1 ribbon falls under both TF5 and TF15 ribbon (Strong Downtrend)….. now check #Kino_CCI_RSI_v5 and look for more than 1 Short trade in a row.

3. When price goes from one zone (say TF1) towards another (say TF5) look for support or resistance on the edges. Look at Chart 2. Usually a zone can be entered by price when a zone is widening and price will be rejected when a zone is narrowing. When a Zone is very narrow resistance/ support will usually be high, though price crosses with ease right at the center crossing of a ribbon (i.e at crossing of ribbon lines of that specific TF ribbon. Most of the time this will be the case with TF1 Ribbon when this happens).

4. Trading in the space between Ribbon Zones (i.e. in black area) usually too presents good trade setup possibilities when price is not (immediately) going to be rejected by a nearby Ribbon or a pivot, etc. The wider the black space between the zones the better the chances for a good trade setup….. yet always verify any trade at the same time with #Kino_CCI_RSI_v5 and strength of divergency.

5. Trading inside a wide opened zone (say TF15) is also possible, For instance when trading GBPJPY you will notice this zone quite often to be very wide. Now when TF1 ribbon has entered and price rises or falls out of TF1 ribbon…… and simultaneously TF5 ribbon being at sufficient distance for price not to be rejected….. price quite often will rise or fall to the other side of the TF15 ribbon. Example 4: Trade starts inside TF15 ribbon on support of both TF1 and TF5 Ribbon.

I have also inserted Kijun 25 Royalblue and Tenkan 13 Red dotted lines for Tradeguidance and optimizing trade entrance and exit.

The dots in the chart are derived from a BraintrendSig indicator which I have modified just a little and called BraintrendSig3.mq4. The number of dots now are highly reduced and the dots that do appear are most of the time in line with the first appearing green or red bar on  #Kino_CCI_RSI_v5 and quite often also in line with the arrows here. Red dots are only useful when in or going in a downtrend. Lime Dots are only useful in the opposite situation..... going up or in an uptrend.

I hope you like this different FX-50 Scalping setup and hopefully it also will contribute to your trading skills and revenues !

BTW the indicators and template are in my next post.

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #1514 ---
It's important to determine why there is not an immediate continuation of a next long here...... and also why there is < so far > no setup for a strong retracement either.

First we see here a block of the Blue CCI..... a breakout to the upside is unlikely...... moreover a breakout above the Gray CCI wouldn't happen close to the zeroline.

An immediate strong retracement is unlikely as well, because TF15 and TF5 zone are still at remarkable distance from price..... so TF5 and TF15 traders presently are still in holding mood and may be looking for their next buy or adding....

So we enter a ranging area and just have to wait for the moment when we see clear signals on the kino_CCI_RSI-v5 that a next opportunity is arriving.

John

--- 帖子 #1515 ---
Another thing is vital in determining valid trades...... when trading between the three TF zones. I call it the minimum required pipdistance , i.e. there must be enough space for price to rise or fall between the TF zones.

How you determine this pipdistance, is shown in the graph.

In this example we see TF5 is going like an opening triangle, which means price will most likely fall through this zone and bounce on the TF15 zone..... next most likely will retrace towards the TF5 zone and bounce here...... next it most likely will try to fall through the TF15 zone.....

This is a scenario which repeats over and over again trading between the TF zones.

Good Luck, John

Hope that makes it clear and may solve your chart problems.

--- 帖子 #1575 ---
To make this or any other Daytrading system more profitable..... you have to look for the major breakouts in a day (24 hrs). Here it is done by watching breakouts above or below all three Ribbons (TF1 TF5 and TF 15 zones).

Say you watch GBPUSD and EURUSD with this sytem for these major Breakouts or High Prob Trades (whats's in a name)..... when you see one occurring on either G/U or E/U.... you immediately start looking if a breakout is going to happen on the other one..... and next on other currency pairs as well....... for most of the time they occur pretty close to one another.

So in that way you actually start SwingTrading as well..... in fact that is what BasketTrading is also based on.

For more on details on this " other currency pairs joining the party " study Radatats method http://www.forex-tsd.com/suggestions...e-mtf-has.html

I can't teach you that.... you have to dig into that really deep yourself !

So..... Good luck in digging more knowledge, John

--- 帖子 #1594 ---
Hi,

Lately there have been quite a number of posts regarding TF5 trading and how good it is to use them with the FX 50 Scalping System...... and I agree 100%..... In fact it is vital to do so.

I thought that everyone who has been trading this system understood that, because right at the beginning of this thread and the previous one started by the Can-Dude, it is mentioned that you have to use the TF5 chart as well.... In fact what we do here or what we should do is, watch the TF5 chart for the breakouts, break of trend...... and next pinpoint the exact entry on the lower Timeframe.... in this case TF1.

If you don't do it this way you almost have to be clairvoyant to pinpoint the right entries.....

Anyway I also have come to the conclusion that a lot of visitors to this thread still do not have the full grasp of what is built in.... in the template I produced on page 100 of this thread.

In fact we have the influence of TF15, TF5 and TF1 built in... in one chart. To make it more clear how to read this chart..... you should have a fresh look at the picture below.

Looking at this chart you may distinguish the spots where the TF15, TF5 and TF1 traders are in agreement..... or are divided in agreement. See how this works out. You can immediately see where for instance TF1 and TF5 traders are going to be in agreement to buy......., ect. In this chart setup you sort of can determine in an analog way what is ahead.....

If you like you can put a (digital= yes/no) confirmation underneath (under the CCI's) like the one Kino published in this thread..... Kino's Has bars....

In the chart below there are two buys completely in agreement with the CCI's and the rules of the FX-50 System. The last one (at the white dotted vertical line) is according to the FX-50 System CCI rules still looking to be a buy...... but now is clearly filtered out by this chart setup >>>>> because of disagreement shown between TF1 -TF5 and TF15 traders !!

Hope this makes it more clear to all of you using this setup

I believe you have something nice to study during the weekend,

Regards, John

BTW. Here is a new template too which uses RandyCandles. I have slightly modified one indicator for better use with the template below. All the other indicators may be found on the pages 100 upto this page of this thread

--- 帖子 #1604 ---
here is the source code for that in mq4

decompiled it, so that you could remove all restrictions if there were any

have fun

-------------------------------

/*

Generated by ForexLion Decompiler

*/

#property copyright "Copyright  2006, FX Sniper"

#property link      ""

#property indicator_separate_window

#property indicator_minimum 0.0

#property indicator_maximum 50.5

#property indicator_buffers 3

#property indicator_color1 Lime

#property indicator_color2 Yellow

#property indicator_color3 Red

double gda_76[];

double gda_80[];

double gda_84[];

double gda_88[];

double gda_92[];

double gda_96[];

extern int limit = 1000;

extern int BarSize = 2;

extern int trh = 10;

int init() {

IndicatorBuffers(8);

SetIndexBuffer(0, gda_84);

SetIndexBuffer(1, gda_88);

SetIndexBuffer(2, gda_92);

SetIndexBuffer(3, gda_76);

SetIndexBuffer(4, gda_80);

SetIndexBuffer(5, gda_96);

SetIndexStyle(0, DRAW_ARROW, STYLE_SOLID, BarSize);

SetIndexArrow(0, 167);

SetIndexDrawBegin(0, limit - 40);

SetIndexStyle(1, DRAW_ARROW, STYLE_SOLID, BarSize);

SetIndexArrow(1, 167);

SetIndexDrawBegin(1, limit - 40);

SetIndexStyle(2, DRAW_ARROW, STYLE_SOLID, BarSize);

SetIndexArrow(2, 167);

SetIndexDrawBegin(2, limit - 40);

SetIndexLabel(0, NULL);

SetIndexLabel(1, NULL);

SetIndexLabel(2, NULL);

IndicatorShortName("SideWinder");

return (0);

}

int deinit() {

return (0);

}

int start() {

int li_32;

double ld_36;

double ld_44;

double ld_56;

double ld_64;

int li_72;

int li_76;

bool li_80;

double ld_88;

double ld_96;

double ld_104;

int li_112;

int li_116;

bool li_120;

double ld_124;

double ld_132;

double ld_140;

int li_148;

int li_0 = TimeDay(TimeCurrent());

int li_4 = TimeMonth(TimeCurrent());

int li_8 = TimeYear(TimeCurrent());

if (li_0 >= 30 && li_4 >= 12 && li_8 >= 2006) {

IndicatorShortName("Outdated Version: Contact fxsniper@gmail.com ");

return;

}

int li_20 = 30;

double ld_24 = 4.0 * MathArctan(1);

for (int li_52 = limit - 26; li_52 >= 0; li_52--) {

ld_44 = 0;

for (int li_12 = 25; li_12 >= 1; li_12--) {

ld_36 = 0;

ld_36 = (li_12 - 8) * (Close[25 - li_12 + li_52]);

ld_44 += ld_36;

}

gda_96[li_52] = 6.0 * ld_44 / 650.0;

}

for (int li_16 = limit; li_16 >= 0; li_16--) {

gda_76[li_16] = iMA(NULL, 0, 34, 0, MODE_EMA, PRICE_CLOSE, li_16);

gda_80[li_16] = gda_96[li_16];

}

for (li_12 = limit; li_12 >= 0; li_12--) {

ld_56 = (Close[li_12 + 1] + (High[li_12 + 1]) + (Low[li_12 + 1])) / 3.0;

ld_64 = 25 / (High[iHighest(NULL, 0, MODE_HIGH, li_20, li_12)] - Low[iLowest(NULL, 0, MODE_LOW, li_20, li_12)]) * Low[iLowest(NULL, 0, MODE_LOW, li_20, li_12)];

li_72 = 0;

li_76 = 1;

li_80 = FALSE;

ld_88 = (gda_76[li_12 + 1] - gda_76[li_12]) / ld_56 * ld_64;

ld_96 = MathSqrt((li_76 - li_72) * (li_76 - li_72) + (ld_88 - li_80) * (ld_88 - li_80));

ld_104 = MathRound(180.0 * MathArccos((li_76 - li_72) / ld_96) / ld_24);

if (ld_88 > 0.0) ld_104 = -1.0 * ld_104;

else ld_104 = ld_104;

li_112 = 0;

li_116 = 1;

li_120 = FALSE;

ld_124 = (gda_80[li_12 + 1] - gda_80[li_12]) / ld_56 * ld_64;

ld_132 = MathSqrt((li_116 - li_112) * (li_116 - li_112) + (ld_124 - li_120) * (ld_124 - li_120));

ld_140 = MathRound(180.0 * MathArccos((li_116 - li_112) / ld_132) / ld_24);

if (ld_124 > 0.0) ld_140 = -1.0 * ld_140;

else ld_140 = ld_140;

if ((ld_104 < trh && ld_104 >= 0.0 && ld_140 + ld_104 >= trh) || (ld_140 < trh && ld_140 >= 0.0 && ld_140 + ld_104 >= trh)) li_32 = 1;

else {

if ((ld_104 > (-trh) && ld_104 <= 0.0 && ld_140 + ld_104 <= (-trh)) || (ld_140 > (-trh) && ld_140 <= 0.0 && ld_140 + ld_104 <= (-trh))) li_32 = 1;

else {

if (ld_104 <= (-trh) && ld_140 <= (-trh)) li_32 = 2;

else {

if (ld_104 >= trh && ld_140 >= trh) li_32 = 2;

else li_32 = 0;

}

}

}

li_148 = 50;

if (li_32 == 2) {

gda_84[li_12] = li_148;

gda_88[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

gda_92[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

}

if (li_32 == 1) {

gda_84[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

gda_88[li_12] = li_148;

gda_92[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

}

if (li_32 == 0) {

gda_84[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

gda_88[li_12] = EMPTY_VALUE;

gda_92[li_12] = li_148;

}

}

return (0);

}

I have been using V2 just like Soeasy does, only with bigger arrows from the 2MA crossover indicator.

Guys, you have to trade on the market overlap times, which you can learn about here http://forex.timezoneconverter.com/, on forex market hours.

There is even the paramount worktime indicator you can setup and make show what are the overlap times on your screen to make it easier.

You got to trade when the markets are open at the same time because then there is more money volume in the market moves, and it makes it easier for a trend to actually happen. CD says to trade 1 hour before and after the market opens, but I have had best results from like 8 AM to 5 PM GMT time. Look into it yourselves, but trade at good hours.

Here is my setup. I'm also with soeasy all the way. Some people will be scared of making pips with a simple system that works, and will be surrounding them with 1000 indicators forever until they get tired of working with something that doesn't work. There are people who look happier playing with indicators than making money and taking it to the bank.

If you can't get good exits on V2, then just go for 10 pips target profit on each trade during overlap times. So many moves going over 30 pips that 10 pip isn't that hard to get when the MAs cross and you get the FXprime red or green bar.

This is a file with everything - indicators, template, instructions, link to videos and documents teaching about market times. More than this I don't know what could help without forcing anyone.

Good luck and good trading! TAKE THE MONEY TO THE BANK!!!

Scalpa

--- 帖子 #1612 ---
Hi,

I am kinda new to forex too. I have only been studying it for around 5 months and learned about FX-Prime V2 last week.

There are good times to trade and bad times. Sometimes you will only get ranges with random trends that give even a good trader a hard time.

There are other times of the day when there are lots of trends that go for many pips, and are easy to catch.

There are also better days of the week and depending on the currency pair, the trends have common trend sizes. It varies a lot of course, but on some days, certain pairs will, for example, have trends that usually go for "at least a Y amount of pips", or a day when the pair will hardly have "trends larger than X pips", because its a day with less activity on the currency.

CD says he trades GBP/USD from 1 hour before to 1 hour after US opens. He says its the best time for his system - the FX-Prime V2. He made it, so he got to know what he is saying.

There are books that say the overlap times are the best times to trade. Some pdf files on the .zip archieve I posted above say exactly this, and also note the best days and hours for each of the main currency pairs.

Myself, I have been watching the charts of what happened the last month and noticed that the best hours to trade - when there is the most volume and the most trends, is between 7 AM and 17 AM GMT. This is when *I* think is the best time to trade the FOREX.

You can look into the MT4, the 5 minute chart all zoomed out for GBP/USD. USD/JPY and EUR/USD and press CTRL+L to see the volume lines. You will note that from 7 AM to 17 AM, there is the most volume and the biggest trends, and that huge trends usually take place in these hours. So that's my experience. Go check things out for yourself.

Do you find it better on the 1 minute or 5 minute timeframe?

I trade on the 1 minute to enter and exit in the best possible moments, but I keep an eye on the 5 minute or larger to see what the trend is, and if there is resistance or support.

and do you have a rigid stoploss or wait for the exit signal?

I think at these market hours you can put a stop of 10 when the V2 gives you a tight MA cross and enter signal. You have to be watching it not to lose money of course, but with so many trends going from 60 to over 100 pips, its easy to win. You can exit on wht Heiken Ashi like CD says on the tutorial and its a great idea. Waiting for the 5 minute trendline to be broken, or put a trail of 25-35 pips depending on the volatility will probably work too.

If you always exit at 40 TP with a trail of 25 pips, and a 10 pip stop, watching the trade, I don't think you will have any problems even if the internet or power goes down. I wouldn't use TP of 40 tough becasue there are so many trends that go over 80 and are signaled well by the Heiken cross, or even another MA cross in the oposite direction.

You could also exit when the FX-Prime green or red bar disappears, but I think it would lead to many early exits. You just gotta know when a trend has ended.

Even if sometimes you exit early or too late - its part of the game. As long ar your account is growing and your taking more money to the bank, there's no reason to care about losses. With time and experience people tend to learn and become better traders with better entries and exits.

The Heiken Aishi will probably be the best option for most people, myself included. Take a look at these things in the last months M5 and M1 charts to see what I am talking about. Be smart and safe, not greedy.

Oh and do you trade with and against the trend/bias?

I would *NEVER* scalp against the trend. Look at the M5 chart or zoom out in the M1 to see the trend, and go with it.

Try the thing on demo first of course, not to lose money. And I don't take responsibility for anything you do. I'm just trying to clear some things out.

This is what I have to say, good luck and lets go get the money hehe!

Scalpa

EDIT: look at screenshots of the period that I trade and how it has good large trends - its the part in black on the charts. Also notice how these periods have larger volume, the green lines underneath. Indigo section is non trade time.

--- 帖子 #1623 ---
Hi,

Yea, I am using !fxprime_v2. If you open all of these indicators at the same chart you will see that many of them are the same thing with a different filename. If the filesize is the same then its likely the same file too... with a different name.

Use a 6 EMA on TF5 to see what the trend is. Put another 12 EMA and when they become close or cross its because the trend has a probability of reversing. Can be like a 5 and 10 EMAs too, like one small average and another larger than it.

I like TF5 better for scalping on TF1. I go to look on larger frames to look for support, larger trends, big formations this type of stuff... Because the larger TF's tendency will overpower the ones in the smaller time frames.

When the trend lines are broken its a good idea to prepare to leave the trade too, specially if its a small profit move...

Good profits!

Scalpa

--- 帖子 #1665 ---
I would like to lay down a few guidlines as I see will help others with trading this system.

Using the ribbons on the screen, along with the CC indicator, here is how I am seeing the best trading scenarios and they all involve trading the lower TF ribbons into the upper TF ribbons, and usually when there is plent of space between them.

Possible examples.

1M into the 5M

5M into the 15M

1M into the 15M

I would not trade in this direction

5M into the 1M

15M into the 1M

15M into the 5M

I would also only make these trades out in space. Which means that if you uploaded the template, I would only trade when you are moving towards blackness on your charts and definitely not when you are inside the rainbow. When you are in the rainbow it is time to get up and take a break.

Now, when using the MACD and divergence, I would take a divergence trade no matter where it occurred. Here is the MACD divergence indicator I am using. Please note that I am using the smoothing lines for signals and not the histogram part. Enjoy and I will be around if you have any questions....

--- 帖子 #1707 ---
The problem with that blanca is that I don't trade by the rules. What JE gave us is a road map to success. I don't ususally make a trade because a line crosses, I usually try to get a feel for the market, and this is not the thread to post that kind of stuff in it. And i have too many other threads I am still managing at the moment to start another one.

Perhaps in time...I will tell you this though..

I have taken JE v2 template and put it on both the 1M and 5M charts. then I take the lowest ribbon on the M5 chart and decide if price is above or below that ribbon. If price is above that ribbon, then i only trade long on the 1M chart and if it is below that ribbon on only trade short on the 1M chart.

I also take no trades on the 1M chart if I am not trading into blackness I don't take the trade. Think of the blackness on the template as either the ocean or the stars. and think of the ribbons as either coral refes or meteror showers. And think of price as your subamarine or your spaceship.

Would you drive your sub into a coral ref or a meteor shower on purpose?

And it is always best if the ribbons are lined up in sequntial order as well. now find a way to feel the market. If the double CCI cross does that for you then use it, if not find somthing else.....

Hope that this is helpful...Damon

Please carefully follow instructions from post 1673 as I stated there:

.......I am happy to do an update with regard to the setup published on pages 100 and 107. Therefore make sure you have already all the indicators listed in my posts on these pages and put them in mt4/experts/indicators map.

--- 帖子 #1745 ---
Brian,

When beginning to use this setup...... why not explicitely look out for the very low risk setups as described on page 100, i.e. those that have all the marks where price is diving into the black abyss (shorts) or rising up to the stars (longs), for by far the best opportunities are to be expected when there is no ribbon under or above the price?

Why choose more risky setups? If you succeed in trading those 50 pips a day trades..... you will have made a lot of money by the end of six months, that is when you use the right scripts for your trade entries and MM as wel....

It's true you may have to wait each day a while, but there is no risk whatsoever in waiting for the right opportunity.

If you want to make more pips you can do the same with for instance GBPUSD.... and grab there the same amount of pips...

Almost every day these opportunities occur..... sometimes more than once. Most of the time these trades make more than 50 pips. Yesterday for instance there was such a beauty starting on EurUSD at about 18:30 GMT. You also could have gotten into this trade at about 18:50 GMT immediately after the first retracement

B.T.W. This is something all of you should be watching. Most of the time the first retracement that occurs..... when going into those black area's presents the better entry on those rides !!!!

This morning such a trade started at 06:21 GMT on EurUSD when price fell under 1.2800 to the Pivotline at 1.2762. A trade like that could have served you well with at least 20 pips.

Only when you have arrived at a point in time where you can distinguish much better and quicker resistance/support you can always go a step further and start trading between and inside the ribbons...

Such would be my advise.

Cheers and have a pipfull day,

John

--- 帖子 #1754 ---
The fact that all TF ribbons are underneath at the spots where you have put the red arrows...... means that the traders on all those TF's still are divided in what to do when price comes down. Indeed there is a double top....

So some will say: Price comes down.

If you look closer you see that the other TF ribbons are underneath.... therefore price has to break through..... The question is: "Will the traders on these TF levels start selling or are they going to hold positions?" In that case price bounces and may go zig zag until it has a chance to breakout above or below all the ribbons >>>> Than you have another trade opportunity.

So the rest of the chart says: This is not a High Prob Trade

B.T.W. You mean it's a triangle which is narrowing I suppose?  That means resistance >>> so it's the first sign that price has difficulty to go down in one line. It may go down at first when the ribbon is a bit wide, however price will come up first and maybe do anther try to go down. We don't go down these messy roads... we preferably take the Highway right into open space...

Only when price is going into wide open black space...... All traders agree to where it's going. The only thing you still have to consider in such cases are nearby Pivotlines and Fiblines.... Price has to cross those too.

The next Pivotline or Fibline...... in open space.... most likely now is the target where price is heading.

Look for all the examples in the pages starting as of page 100 upto this page. Study those over and over again !!!

Good Luck, John

--- 帖子 #1778 ---
The breakout in the middle of this chart is valid, because of divergency on CCI's. Notice how it has made a zig-zag formation before steaming higher.

Look at the breakout at the end..... how different this one is in respect with the one in the middle.

The breakout at the end of the chart already lost all it's upward potential at the final breakout to continue.....  there is no retracement back towards the upper ribbon. Price falls immediately under the ribbon...... So it has to make total new run in order to get above the ribbon again......

Also notice how far it went already in a straight line. Divergency on CCI's is not available here. So this is not a valid breakout.

Study all the valid examples on the previous pages starting at page 100 and you will develop an eye for this >>>> Next time you spot immediately if a breakout is valid.

Hope this helps you, John

im not a coder but i found in another mq4 something that may or can be added i think ??? Maybe Kino or someone else can add that option would be cool to add a sound of star wars in it  but thats really optionnal any sound will give you your attention to check your monitor for a possible trade to take

Inserted Code extern string           Alert_Setting        = "---------- Alert Setting";
extern bool             EnableAlert          = true;
extern string           SoundFilename      = "alert.wav";
Inserted Code //----------------------- SOURCE :
void subCrossAlert(string type)
{
string AlertComment;

if(type=="UP")   AlertComment = "blah blah blah !";
if(type=="DOWN") AlertComment = "blah !";

Alert(AlertComment);
PlaySound(SoundFilename);
}

--- 帖子 #1858 ---
great post lloydy and try to sit aside when it gets whipsawing if possible. Also plus pips are plus pips. If you take a trade and you see that a very smart and high probability exit is 15 pips, unless it blows right threw that level. take the 15, be happy(were scalping on the 1 min chart), then wait on the next clean set up and go at it again. If I feel 15 pips is my smartest exit I'll take it any day and not care at all if it runs another 10 pips or what ever. This is just the way I handle exits because exits were the hardest part of a trade for myself. It's like flying a plane, takeing off is optional, but landings are not.

--- 帖子 #1864 ---
It's nice to see many new visitors to this thread and also other traders that want to use a bit of our technique in their systems and setups..... The more visitors the better I think, for the worst death threat to a thread is..... when there is not much going on anymore....

Indeed I am pleased to see that we are still alive and kickin' here....

Okay here is the update I promised last week.

On both templates FXprime_V2-JE.mq4 is being used the same way..... Upper FXprime with faster CCI settings and lower FXprime with slower CCI settings. Both are tweaked in such a way that when the dots on the lower FXprime appear this may be taken as an alert...

I am not going to explain how to use FXprime for there are plenty of posts in this thread that convey all of that. The only thing to be mentioned, although quite obvious is: When the lower FXprime is red and the upper FXprime becomes Red too.... this marks possible entries for Shorts that should be examined further. The same for Longs of course: When the Lower FXprime is Green and the upper FXprime becomes Green as well this marks possible entries for Longs that should be examined further.

Simultaneously we look at what price is doing: Is it coming free from the ribbons? What is the pipdistance towards the next Ribbon or to a Fibo- or Pivot-level?

Simultaneously we look at the DoubleCCI-With_SMA. This one has already been published in this thread some months ago, but comes in quite handy with this setup using FXprime_V2 Final-JE.mq4 twice.

As a rule when using DoubleCCI-With_SMA in this setup you may do the following:

Usually good entries occur for long...... when CCI is above +67 and above SMA..... Most of the time marked by a retracement of the CCI back towards the SMA and/or +67 line. Under all circumstances look for divergencies in the prelude to an entry.....

Usually good entries occur for short..... when CCI is below-67 and below SMA.... Most of the time marked by a retracement of the CCI back towards the SMA and/or -67 line. Under all circumstances look for divergencies in the prelude to an entry....

The first template has the settings of the ribbons first used and published on page 100 of this thread. B.T.W. Besides the ones you find beneath the Chartgraph....... You need all the indicators of all my posts on page 100. If you wish to use BrainTrend4Sig, MACandles or Randy Candles on the chart.... They are available in the templates as well. Right click on the chart and change the Vizualisation setting from Monthly to All Timeframes. You may also have to change the ChartOnForeground setting. To do this right click on the chart and look for this setting in the Properties window (F8).

The JE-Bar_Trend.mq4 you'll find in post #1601. Some indicators may be found in post #1673 and the MACandles.mq4 is in post #1754

The second template uses slightly different settings and has another TF zone added. I.E. in this template there now are 4 TF zones..... TF1, TF5, TF15 and TF30. This has been done because the TFzones are a bit faster here and therefore we now need TF30 as well. The advantage is that exits now are marked a bit earlier as well. The Kijun-Tenkan is being used for tradeguidance.

The rules for using this second template are not different from the ones published on page 100 !!

The Kijun/Tenkan also helps identifying entries and exits when it exits/enters the TF1 zone ribbon almost simultaneously with price.

Another difference compared to the previous Ribbon settings (in all previous templates) quite often now apppears at entries, i.e. second chance entries (often also better entries) may occur after the first retracement of price back towards Zones TF1, TF5 and TF15 at the same moment, i.e. when TF1,TF5 and TF15 zones are (very) close together.

In the chart below there are two examples how to determine entries.

Hope you like it.....

John

--- 帖子 #1882 ---
To me this looks too early, because the SMA is still negative. Furthermore you didn't wait for the pullback towards +67 or in this case the zeroline?

This chart however shows an excellent opportunity for a long at around 21:34 hrs.

1. First the Alert White Dots on Lower FXPrime-V2 at around 21:10, which is twenty minutes before the actual long opportunity took place

2. Next notice two short breaks on green Upper FXPrime V2 (these are in fact very short retracements; last one occurs at about 21:34)

3. Price retraces towards Kijun/Tenkan and TF1 zone simultaneously at 21:34

Now you look for confirmation....... for a valid pullback on the CCI. And there it is:

At that same moment CCI-89 is green and falls back below SMA and +67 line. Than few minutes later.... CCI starts rising again above +67 and SMA.

Just before that you enter for long.

Als note that Price didn't even enter the TF1 Zone or the Kijun-Tenkan !!

Look for that kind of opportunities.

Good Luck, John

--- 帖子 #1887 ---
Someone posted recently.and I agree, the best trades are when the ribbons agree. Ie the ribbon we are on 1 min and the 5 min tf both show up

when you are entering long, or both show down when entering short.

The times I see this as not a factor in my decision to enter is when

price is approaching a higher tf resistance for example, ie price is

approaching the 15 min ribbon and there is no support immediately

below.. the stronger resistance above overcomes the tf 5 ribbon

agreeing or not.  And second.. in any position basically where the

5 ribbon is very thin.  It does not need to agree if the 5 ribbon

is very thin at the time of entry, it provides very little real resistance

to consider.

Any thoughts anyone based on your trades?

thanks

Brian

--- 帖子 #1894 ---
Forex scalping is the art of using high leverage and a large number of short term trades to steadily increase an account. Usually, only 1 to 5 pips are targeted for each trade. This type of trading appeals greatly to day traders and those looking to minimize the risk involved in trading currencies. Next to money management, “risk control” is the single most important trait to a surviving (and thriving) currency trader. The small amount of time that is spent in the market limits much of the risk in exposure in comparison to a longer term system. Also, the freedom involved in a speedy Forex scalping system in such a liquid market is a “magnet” that drives many traders from other markets to try their hand in currency. A disciplined and steady scalper could seamlessly double or triple an account, and spend only a fraction of the time in the market as a common day trader.

If you found this introduction interesting read the rest of the article Forex Trading Methods - Scalping

--- 帖子 #1940 ---
It' very nice to see you all saw this trade coming and did take good profits.

Nevertheless I would like to point out to new visitors to this thread how easy it is to see this kind of High Prob Trade coming. Especially when using the latest V3.2 template.

All remarks are on the chart. Really it's that simple to spot a high prob trade.

One thing you should always look at when using template v3.2 because it is most significant when pinpointing entries is the following:

When the Kijun/Tenkan joins in a horizontal move one of the Ribbon lines of TF1 zone (CornflowerBlue and DeepPink) and price falls or rises through this combo, it's a first indication for entries. Of course this has to be validated by the rest of the chart (CCI and FXPrime's). Try to develop an eye for this !!.

What you could do is, run through several charts to check if there is some truth in this statement or..... how valuable it is when making entry decisions. I leave that up to you...

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #1943 ---
When Price falls in such a way as it did about 09:13...... there is almost always a second repetitive trade coming according to Elliot Wave theory.

The first one starting at a point 2 (being a Wave 3) and the second trade starting at a point 4 (being a Wave 5). In this case that became true as well.

Usually the Wave 5 trade is not that big as the Wave 3..... which became true here as well. But still a nice 70-80 pips ride...

So be aware next time you see a downfall like this..... there is a very good chance for the repetitive Trade.

It's all in the chart.

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #1955 ---
Hi Pipster,

On this chart there are some possibilities you may have look at:

1. The trendline on the chart, either drawn on price or drawn along side the Kijun/Tenkan. The cross provides an exit. However when you expect a possible bounce of Price (in this case made visual by Randy Candles) on the TF1 zone, you may decide to let it run. An other possibility is.... Place two short positions when beginning a High Prob Trade...... Close 1 trade when you feel unsecure at this point and .... Let the other one run and see if it develops further in your favor..... as would heave been the case here.

2. The upper FXPrime most of the time also provides good exits as you can see.

3. Another exit strategy is provided by the SMA. When Short.... SMA under the -67 line turning up from a trendline over the latest part of the SMA. You see an opening is being created with all exits.

4. Another one is provided by the blue BrainTrend4Sis dots.

Your question about entering a short above a single Pivot- or Fibline only can be done when there has been a bounce of price shortly before on that Fibline. If not don't go ahead and wait until you have seen a bounce. The next retry for Price to go down usually succeeds...... at least when there is nothing else in the way (i.e. Fib- Pivotline or ribbons).

Continuation of Price in the same direction as it did go before....... is especially most likely when Price now falls out of a triangle shape.... or rises up from from a triangle shape when price is rising of course.

Price falling out of or rising from a triangle always has some boost power to cross ribbons, Pivot- and Fiblines. There are four examples on this chart for re-entry this way. Take care that at the narrowing point of the triangle you see at least one bounce on either side before price starts breaking out of the triangle !!

Hope this helps, John

--- 帖子 #1965 ---
Hi Kino,

You are right. Maybe your insights are different from the ones I have, but I hope analyzing the matter early this morning is helpfull. I have studied few examples where TF1 zone crosses above or under all other Zones. Indeed these are not all the same and certainly this doesn't happen all the time when TF30zone is being crossed, because one of the other zones (TF5, TF15) may already be above or under TF30).

So the priciple for this indic could be like this: If a crossing of TF1 occurs with any of the ribbons of the other zones at a certain price level...... simultaneously this indic checkes if the other zones are above or below that price level....

Say a crossing of one of the ribbons of TF1 zone occurs with one of the ribbons of TF15 (with Eurusd) at 1.3225....... next the indicator has to check whether TF5 and TF 30 are above or below this price level.

A crossing above this price level indicates a possible Long High Prob Trade range. A crossing below this price level now would indicate a possible Short High Prob Trade. Crossing back between any of the TFzones would mean a Non High Prob Trade range

Next A finetuning is necessary to secure early entries at these levels by having the check of the fastest zone (TickZone) crossing above or below TF1zone. This finetunecheck however also could be done by using the Kijun/Tenkan. It could even be better to use the Kijun/Tenkan for the finetunecheck.

So it is more difficult to create a reliable sensor indicator than we thought at first glance..... What do you think of it Kino?

John

--- 帖子 #1969 ---
Right now happening on EursUsd. Two successive Shorts. Same principle as on last Friday.

Using triangles alongside the ribbons provides another very powerful tool to determine entries. To do so.....  you draw two of the sides exactly alongside the (lower) ribbons of the TFzones as on this chart.

The upper TFzones "press" price down.... so this a strong indication for price to fall out of the triangle. When it does..... There is your short opportunity!

There are some more examples of this on last Fridays chart.

Cheers and have a pipfull week, John

--- 帖子 #1970 ---
Nice to see people thinking about developing an alert indicator. Here are my thoughts.

We have two types of High Prob trades.
case 1. if price is between ribbons with enough pipdistance.....etc
case 2. if price is under/above all TF ribbons

general measurement: check for all TF Ribbon(1,5,15,30) if Ribbon minus price is positive or negative. So this are 4 checks. The 4 results are
a1 = negative or positive

a5 = negative or positive
a15= negative or positive
a30= negative or positive

In case 1. the indi compares
a.) if a1=positive, than check if pipdistance between price and Ribbons with negative results (a5, a15, a30) >35 pips. If yes, print red.
b.) if a1=negative, than check if pipdistance between price and Ribbons with positive results (a5, a15, a30) >35 pips. If yes, print green.

In case 2. the indi compares

if a1 AND a5 AND a15 AND a30 are positive; if yes print red
if a1 AND a5 AND a15 AND a30 are negative; if yes print green

-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Why do I say price? Because only than you have an early warning. That gives you the opportunity to make your homework on your entry decision.

I repeat this sentence of John:
Next A finetuning is necessary to secure early entries at these levels by having the check of the fastest zone (TickZone) crossing above or below TF1zone. This finetunecheck however also could be done by using the Kijun/Tenkan. It could even be better to use the Kijun/Tenkan for the finetunecheck.

I am not sure if the indicator should make such an examination for us. What do we want? We want an alert that tells us if there is a possible high prob entry. I think we should look if precise conditions  are good enough for entry by ourselfs. It's not an EA...

factor1:           0.72

If you you closer Jazz you will notice that the Kijun/Tenkan is just outside the TF1zone, making a weird jump and certainly not close alongside one of the ribbons or inside the the TF1 zone.

4. There were already three shorts in a row, which usually marks the end of a complete Elliot Wave .

--- 帖子 #1981 ---
Here we have a "cup and saucer " shape, Usually these are much wider in shape, but nevertheless you also can identify it as V-shape with two arms. The arm on the right hand falls just under the TF5Zone after two bounces marked by the small circles.

This is a very powerful shape. First of all it identifies a trend reversal..... the end of an Elliot Cycle and the beginning of a new Elliot Cycle. When you see it occur there is always boost power right at the moment when price rises up or falls down from this right arm. I once read on some trading forum that this could be referred to as NOAH's arm and hand...... Out of the hand the pigeon flies up in the sky !

Here it is particularly nice to see the making of it just under a TF5 Zone and and breaking right into it and above it..... straight up towards the TF15 zone.

Just wanted to share this, John

--- 帖子 #1990 ---
Hi Wheel,

The V3.1 template uses one more Zone..... an even faster zone than the TF1 Zone. This one is only used to pinpoint entries with regard to the TF1 Zone and it is also used for tradeguidance, i.e. when you entered a trade it helps you to find the exit point of the trade.

The V3.2 template doesn't use this faster Zone. Instead of that we here use the Kijun/Tenkan to help us pinpoint entries and exits. When using this template you look for the first retracement after price has crossed the TF1Zone above or below one of the other Zones. There you most of the time find the best entry points, i.e. most of the time this will be just above or below the TF5Zone. At this same moment you take care that pipdistance towards another TFzone, Pivot- or Fibline is more than 35 pips away.

When price doesn't see any of these zones below or above it..... you than have a great chance for entering a High Prob Trade.

Yesterday I changed the settings for TF1Zone on this V3.2 template when using triangles to help find entries. You will find these settings in one of my latest posts  in this thread. Also you will find several examples how to draw and use these triangles.

This is the way how I now use template V3.2.

In the chart below there is an example of such a retracement. Pipistance towards the lower TFZone is a little less than 35 pips, however the retracement is a perfect one. Secondly the Kijun/Tenkan is horizontal over a relative long distance inside the TF1 Zone and price has no chance of getting above the Kijun/Tnkan. Next there is a yellow dot of the BrainTrend4Sig very close to price just under the TF1Zone.

Further validation is found on the CCI crossing zero and SMA already under zeroline. Upper (fast) FXprime is red and Lower (slow)FXprime shows a white dot.....

Hope this makes it clear,

John

--- 帖子 #1991 ---
Yesterday's V-shape trade example is a bit different from the one we saw happening here...

This V-Shape has two short arms left and on the right hand we see one short arm (trial for breakout) and the next one succeeds the breakout.

As the story goes NOAH gave the pigeon a trial flight first (first trial for breakout on the right)...... however the pigeon returned with a little branch..... (indicating it won't be long anymore). The next time NOAH let the pigeon fly..... it went up in the sky and it didn't return !!!

I like this aphorism so much...

When you have developed an eye for this powerfull V-Shape setup...... You'll see them happening again and again.

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #2013 ---
Hi Pipster,

You didn't make a very wrong entry here..... however you may next time consider the following:

1. TF1 zone is crossing above TF5zone..... not TF1zone is retracing towards and next taking off again above TF5zone. Sometimes a crossing may be Okay, f.i. when shortly before TF1zone started taking off from TF15zone immediately under TF5zone.

2. In this chart however price has come a long way already.... look at CCI how long it has been green... so the question is how much renewal force may be expected at this point in time for price to make another break through?

Next there is a Pivotline very close above or near to your entry point. Price has not yet come above the Pivotline and make a retracement back towards...... and after such a retracement stayed above that Pivotline.

Think of Pivotlines on TF1 charts not being a single line.... but as an area with 5 - 7 pips (depending on currencypair) on both sides where price still may fall back under the Pivotline or rise above it again.... if price dropped just under that Pivotline.

Remember these same Fib- and Pivotlines are also used by other traders on TF30, TF60, TF240, ect. On those timeframes 5 -7 pips is hardly to be seen as an area on both sides....

3. TF1 Zone on this chart has not quite recently made a connection with any of the TFzones..... as such that TF1 zone bounced an started rising above that zone. That sort of connection happened a while ago at about 17:06 hrs, where TF1zone fell into TF15 zone. Next you see TF1zone rise above TF15 zone >>>> This is important for right at this moment TF1 and TF15 traders are in agreement to start buying respectively hold their positions.

TF5 traders however are still waiting what price is going to do. As you can see TF5zone is hoovering above TF1 and TF15zone. So for TF5 zone traders now the question is..... will price rise above the TF5 zone level..... or will it not be able to cross and will price start dropping from this TF5 level...... when price reaches this level? You better avoid these kind of situations.

If price drops at this level it means TF5 traders are are not going ahead with TF1Zone and TF15Zone traders, but they start taking profits. If on the other hand price continues to rise it means that TF5 zone trades join the club and at least hold their positions or also start buying/adding to their positions. Usually in a situation like this you will see price continuing to rise after some hesitation, which is the case here as well.

If it were the other way around... think of it as if TF5zone and TF15zone were in each others place.... it would have been much more more difficult for price to rise above TF15 level.

Anyway the better trade setups arrive when TF1 zone is completing a retracement towards TF5 (or TF15) zone and both are above the other zones. Immediately when price now takes off from TF1zone and there is no Pivot- or Fibline obstrucion you enter for long. Same goes for short the other way around of course.

As Jazz stated this trade could have gone the right way, but I also think you expected price to continue to rise immediately and therefore you had put in a tight stoploss or closed yourself the trade a little too early. Look at the Red Randy Candle still above the Kijun/Tenkan as your tradeguider..... and indeed next prise continued to rise.

Hope this helps, John

Two examples which happened today shortly afterwards the first part of my reply...... exactly fit this reply and whereas a picture tells more than a 1000 words...... here is that chart to prove it !!! For this I made use of Jazz1964 template.

B.T.W. If you make two or three trades a week according to this setup..... you may say goodbeye to your boss.....

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #2018 ---
You entered on the blue dot and red arrow. Next price came down..... however the third red candle didn't go under the Kijun/Tenkan.... Next price went up again.

Pivotlines are important, however they are far less strong and important than the TFZones, certainly when both are in the same area and support or resistance is being added by the TFZones.

TFZones show you more than anything else how support and resistance is being built up in a chart and it does that by taking care of the influences of 5 TF's in one chart, i.e. TickZone + TF1, TF5, TF15 and TF30.

Look for instance at the chart I did add to the previous answer regarding your trade setup. You will notice..... on that chart I have neglected some of those Pivots- and Fiblines, because they are completely overruled by the force of the TFZones. TFZones building support here in this way..... is the main issue that counts and overrules everything else in any chart in such moments.

If you study and learn this trade setup by heart..... you will next time immediatley recognize when it it arrives.

No need to change anything with any broker using this template or trade with any manual trade system, unless you have a broker that applies Floating Spread (which in such cases may vary from 2 to 25 pips) at irregular intervals. Brokers that use Floating pipspread are thieves. Avoid these type of brokers.... as if they are the Plague, cause they are.....

Broker issues normally only are of a different kind and f.i. require the right scripts for getting in and of trades.

Good Luck, John

--- 帖子 #2023 ---
I am glad you asked this question, because what you tell us by this is basically the mistake made by most traders. They look for entries at the indicators underneath. That is never the way to make an entry decision.

What I want to point out to you is:

When it is not in the chart..... it certainly is not in the indicators underneath. By this I mean, that you have to read any chart as such that the chart itself conveys to you which is an entry and which is not an entry point..... which is an exit and which is not.

What really matters all the time in any chart is the game of support and resistance, attraction and rejection. That is the name of the game and it is in the chart alone. You have to develop an eye for that...... using MA's TFzones, Pivot- and Fiblines, etc.

Any indicator underneath.... never ever should be more than a confirmation indication. Sometimes you see charts with more than 7 indicators underneath.... all telling the same story. These only mess up reading a chart and never contribute reading a chart immediately when necessary!!!!

The rest already has been answered by Jazz,

Hope this helps too,

John

--- 帖子 #2038 ---
I want to show you the results of a visual backtest. I did research on EURUSD with the v3.1 template. Testperiod March 5th to April 6th, equal to 22 trading days.

FIRST backtest: PRICE above or under ALL TF RIBBONS:

For this type of trade I searched for situations where

1. price broke out from all TF Ribbons,

2. price made a pullback to the TickRibbon

3. and after that price went away from TickRibbon

4. AND ALSO TickRibbon broken out from other TF Ribbons.

Profitable:   30

Breakeven/Loss: 21

Total trades: 51

Win %    59%

Conclusion:

Though winning%>50% we can't speak about an high probability trade.

SECOND backtest: TF1 RIBBON above or under OTHER TF RIBBONS:

For this kind of entry the next terms are concerned:

1. TF1 is breaking out of other TF Ribbons

2. TickRibbon on the good side of TF1 Ribbon

3. Price on the good side of TickRibbon

Profitable: 18

Breakeven/Loss: 4

Total trades: 22

Win %  82%

Conclusion:

Entry on this type of breakout is certainly a high probabilility trade.

THIRD backtest: Trading between the Ribbons:

Following conditions were indicative:

1. price and TickRibbon both on good side of TF1 Ribbon

2. Tickdistance between price and TF5/TF15 Ribbon should be at least 30 pips.

3. If pipdistance to the next Ribbon was not big enough, but if it concerned a good widening triangle, I also 'took the trade'.

Profitable: 40

Breakeven/Loss: 13

Total trades: 53

Win %  75%

Conclusions:

When TF1 breaks out from the other TF Ribbons, we have an high prob opportunity.

Trading opportunities between the ribbons occures often and they give high probability trade possibilities.

Reading the thread, I am getting the impression that Trading Between The Ribbons does not get the attention that it deserves.

Following pictures shows an exemple of each backtest type.

"disclaimer": it was hard to do an exact test, so please don't ask me the testing data. The results that I post here are more or less reliable, but still indicative.

--- 帖子 #2042 ---
Hello Art, welcome to MT4 and this forexfactory community of Friends!

You don't need to attach the indicators on your chart. If an EA is using internal indicators like atr, rsi, stochs, etc, it can get that data from MT4 internally. If it's using external custom indicators they'll need to be in your indicator folder and they need to be compiled.

When you downloaded all indicators which you found in relation to the EA, than they will be compiled almost for sure.

Have fun.

--- 帖子 #2055 ---
Many of us have started the same way..... and I agree a simple chart is often better than a complicated chart with too many indicators and certainly underneath.

As you stated having read the whole thread, I conclude that you are willing to study and invest in knowledge.

The advantage of using TFZones over other Trading Systems is that you can quite clearly see where there is going to be support and resistance. TFZones show you dynamic support and resistance, i.e. it shows you where these are to be expected in relation to both time and price. Fibo- and Pivotlines only show price levels as horizontal lines.

Actually the TickZone (fastest zone) and the next one TF1Zone in the V3.1 template do more or less the same as the basic indicators indicators on your chart.

Trading is not only a matter of getting entries and exits right, but also very much needs "target determination", i.e. at the moment you pull the trigger you also need to have some idea of how far that trade may go.....

There are many systems being used for target determination, like trendlines, fibs, pivots, Elliot Wave, Wolfewave, etc. TFzones too come in quite handy here..... you don't have to draw anything..... they simply are there all the time in each and every chart. Of couse you have to study how it works or maybe also have to get used to it, but than that is no different from any other trading system...

So what you could do is set up another chart as well using TFZones and switch between charts. Jazz1964 also trades that way.... Maybe that helps you to discover the power of the TFZones.

Good Luck, John

--- 帖子 #2072 ---
Kino

Your new indicator nicely signals arrival of Major Breakouts and High Prob Trades. Here is a new template. Added are the TF30 zone and also #Spudfibo and ZigZagPointer. The #Kino_close_above_ribbons indicator doesn't take the TF30Zone into acount, therefore "above all ribbons means here above TickZone + TF1Zone + TF5Zone + TF15Zone. You will notice that TF30Zone is of less importance for entry decision and actually is more or less only usefull to identify support and resistance at greater distances. As such the edges of TF30Zone (=TF30Ribbon) most of the time work more the same as Pivot-and Fiblines.

The #Kino_close_above_ribbons indicator does indeed point to a breakout at hand. In this case there are 2 breakout trials above all ribbons that stop under the #SpudFibo line..... the third one succeeds.

Now this very important: The 3-d one is the one you want to have to enter your trade... Why? This is the only breakout that fullfils all requirements at point 4, because here TF1Zone (CornflowerBlue and DeepPink coloured edges) is rising after a retracement first...... above all other TFZones and simultaneously the TickZone (DarkGreen and DarkOrange edge) has made a small retracement from above towards TF1 Zone.

This fullfilment is the reason why now Price breaks above the #SpudFibo line and Price will continue to rise untill it reaches the next level of resistance..... most of the time provided by next level of Fibo or Pivotlines.

Kino's new indicator beautifully marks the entry point together with the break in the upper FXPrime_V2 indicator.

ZigZagPointer is only being used to point forward to possible valid entry points marked by the BrainTrend4Sig.

There is however one snag using #Kino_above_ribbons. I think because of the Ribbons it uses quite a lot of CPU or of graphical display and therefore slows downs MT4 performance...... So Kino if you could change that by using the simple T3MA indicator for this purpose in your #Kino_above_ribbons indicator...... that might solve the MT4 performance issues.

B.T.W. Looking forward to the .mq4 version.

Anyway here is the chart to prove the breakout example, a new template + ZigZagpointer + #Spudfibo.

All other indicators necessary for this template can be found on page 100 of this thread

Hope you like it, John

[quote=ClearTrade;2661768]Hi Guys

I'm really thinking about going fulltime with trading forex even though I only have less than 1 year experience

---------

Hi ClearTrade,

Trading full time in the future is my personal goal too. At the moment, I'm still learning the markets and getting a feel of it.  I've got this advice from a friend/ trading mentor to share....Hope you find it useful as well.

Satini

-------------------------------------------------------------------
How to become a full time trader, slowly

Many people wonder how you start out as a full time trader.  There are probably many ways, but here is a way that helps you not sabotage yourself and stay realistic. I have to assume that you are already working, or at least have money to trade.

1.         Before trading full time, you need at least a years worth of income. That means all monthly bills, plus a nest egg in savings, or other liquid instruments. Lets say it is $100,000.

2.         If you are working, that income can pay the bills. Do not depend on trading to do that yet.

3.         After you learn a trading system, build your account using leverage. Open your account with the necessary money needed to trade one mini, or one standard. Let's say it is $1,000 in a mini account.

4.         As you get better and gain skill, you will begin making money. When you have made $1,000, begin trading two lots.  Do not remove any money from your account.  When you make $1,000 more, add another lot. Continue doing this, until you have $100,000 in your account, or whatever your yearly income is.

5.         It's not time to quit your job yet.  If you need $100,000 a year for bills, you need $2,000 a week, assuming a 50 week work year.

6.         Now you need to see if you can do that.   To do that, first, treat trading like a business. Go to work, shut the door, and trade, for the allotted amount of time, during the day. Focus only on trading the rules. Do not make it a goal to make $2,000 a week. If you focus on the money you will make mistakes. Some weeks you will make $4,000, and some weeks only may make $500. It's the average that matters.  Take what the market gives you daily. You can't force it.  If you are in a trade and have made your $2,000 and just exit, you have not traded the rules correctly. That trade could have gone on and made you $8,000.

7.         Now, after six months or so you have consistently made your goal, then consider trading full time.  Keep in mind that your expenses will increase.  Insurance, no IRA, taxes.  Your broker submits a 1099 to the IRS every January.  A CPA can tell you more about how to structure yourself correctly. Just withdraw the $2,000 per month or more for savings or a Roth IRA.  Keep at least $100,000 in your account so you never feel like you are losing money, and start worrying.

8.         The rest of the stuff, like advantages and disadvantages of self-employment, dealing with isolation, etc, you will just need to figure that out on your own. It is individual for everyone.

--- 帖子 #2106 ---
LS,

It's nice to see colouring the TFZones, when it helps you identifying the different Zones easier this way.

No there is not a very special reason why I gave the ribbons a different colour. The only thing is the coloured ribbons do visually immediately identify the slower T3MA of a TFZone, where price most of the time enters a TFZone and also leaves a TFZone. But this is not true all the time.

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #2107 ---
Hi Kino,

This example chart looks great Kino!

Good to see you have found time to work on this strategy. You're such a good coder, we owe you so much..... many many thanks!!

I would like to give some remarks.

1) In my opinion R1 is to slow for identifying good scalping trade setups. So my suggestion is to use RTick or Price. I think RTick is the best solution. John, what is your thought?

2) The upper and the lower Ribbon on which distance should be calculated can be R5 or R15, just depending on which Ribbons are neighbours. John, what is your thought? R1?

3) As JE allready brought to attention, it would be nice if you could add a numerical display of the distances, I think on the right side of the indicator window. So you could read it if the chart is shifted by the chart shift button. I have made a note on the chart example.

4) I am asking myself if this indicator can replace the close above ribbons indicator. The best trade setups when price is <> all ribbons is if RTick did go under or above the other Ribbons. In these cases your indi which is in preperation would give:

- solely blue bars if RTick is above all ribbons (indi value>zero)

- solely red bars (indi value< zero, if RTick is below all ribbons)

- blue AND simultaneously red bars if RTick is between the Ribbons, only draw these bars if there is enough pipdistance to one of the ribbons. The distance should be calculated to the nearest flanks

- no signal bars if RTick is inside any of the other ribbons, and if price is between the ribbons while pipdistance is too small.

5) Using Rtick instead of Price above/under Ribbons .....gives the advantage that the indicator gives cleaner signals and later on .... cleaner/less sound and text alerts.........Too many alerts isn't fine......Otherwise a time delay should be added which adjust that the indicator shouldn't give a new signal within x minutes after the last signal (in the same direction).

6) Using Rtick instead of Price above/under Ribbons .....gives the disadvantage that signals will come later on, so you have less time to make your homework for trade entry.

The chartexample which I attached is just a hand drawn trial. It's not really okay. Kino or John, If you need a better/clearer one, just ask.

--- 帖子 #2114 ---
Hi LSs,

sorry for rudely quoting your post

I saw your question on your chart. here is my answer.

The 3 TF ribbons are coming together from different directions and all traders have to decide what they think price will go to do. Some were long and some others were short. So it can take some time before the decision for the next direction is taken, and it could also go to a sideways market for a while.

On the first point you marked TF1 is going up and price is going down, with a gap between these two.

At your second mark, TF1 is much better situated. Better in relation to price and better in relation to higher TF ribbons. Here it is more likely that price will going to fall.

Overall, in case of a reversal it is better if TF1 is falling out of the bigger TF zones and TickRibbon makes a pullback to TF1 zone.

I noticed this is a chart from februari. You're really doing a huge backtest!

--- 帖子 #2138 ---
Hi LSs,

nice to see you busy with this system!

Rising TF5 and TF15 are indications for a possible continuation of uptrend. The widening TF5 indicates that support is not too strong, so don't take position when price is in this zone. It's not clear what will happen, it's just a game between TF5 traders ....and TF1 traders!

Yes that's true. But the fifference between the pdf chart and yours is the position of TF1 zone. Also CCI divergence indicates less strength on the down movement. Lower FXPrime indicator...missing short signal.

So there are several indications that price could go up again. If you took the short, here is your exit. (I can't see it very sharp, but it looks like pipdistance was good enough for a short entry)

Long entry is drawn in my chart.

Good luck LSs!

--- 帖子 #2139 ---
Hello eegle,

maybe you have to many history bars on the ribbons in your template.

Try to check and if needed: change in MetaEditor the settings of the kino_t3ma ribbon filled indicator

Change the i factor into 2000 or even 1000.

Goto your navigator folder,

rightclick on the indicator,

2nd position: Edit

look for this setting and if it is too big, change this:

for(i=2000; i>=0; i--)

// iCustom( string symbol, int timeframe, string name, ..., int mode, int shift)

don't forget to compile the change you have made by pressing the compile button and wait for message that it is okay.

restart MT4

You can give this a try. Good luck!

--- 帖子 #2140 ---
If you are using any of Kino's Close_above_ribbons indicators..... Detach all of them, because all those indicators are in need of a modification with regard to filling up the logfile under MT4/experts dramatically..... ultimately slowing down your computer to standstill when all space one your harddrive has been consumed.

To get rid of this problem:

1. Detach those indicators from all charts

2. Close down MT4.

3. Next open MT4/experts/logs and delete all the logfiles you see there. (B.T.W. Could be Gigabyte files !!!!)

4. Restart MT4 and check the experts Tab on the MT4 Terminal window if you still see any continues repeating messages.....  which shouldn't be the case now.

5. Have patience and wait for Kino's upgraded version.

Cheers, John

LSs,

First of all.... Thank you very much for posting these examples.... for there simply is no better way of teaching yourself trading..... than by posting your trade examples... whether you succeeded or not at that moment doesn't matter. Next time you always do (a little) better !!!! Ultimately this adds up to become a very succesful trader. THX !!!

TF30Zone is at times the widest of them all.... Therefore it offers possibilities to trade inside its bounderies. Where it says on your chart: "Would anyone take this trade?".... it's obvious you are to late to enter.

It's not my favorite one..... You could however have entered a long right at the bottom TF30Zone ribbon where price rises up from TF1Zone. Why? There has been a bounce to Yellow TF5Zone...... so it is now very likely that inside TF30Zone next time price will break through TF5Zone..... as indeed it does here !!

My favorite entry however would be right at the end of this chart.... where price is thrown up from Flipper's nose.... (as if this dolphin is throwing a ball into the air)..... recognize this pattern? Watch it... How strong the first candle is at this nose point when price jumps higher.... You see this funny little Flipper Nose Pattern over and over again with TFZones........ and where it appears it's most of the time quite good for entries. B.T.W Pipdistance towards your Blue TFZone is about 35 pips. So this is a nice scalp.

Also good to check what CCI is doing: It's green and nicely crossing above SMA..... Also both FXPrime's are green..... This is an entry by the book !!

Could you post a chart.... how it went from there?

Hope this helps, John

--- 帖子 #2153 ---
LSs,

The longer you work with TFZones the easier it gets.... for you will develop an eye for the entries (plus exits). Actually you can see this short developing for a while.

Where it says: "TF30 seem to resist again" in fact price is bouncing back on heavy resistance of both upper ribbon of TF30Zone (magenta) and lower ribbon of TF15 (blue-ish), i.e. the gray zone in between those ribbons shows a triangle narrowing resistance area. At the crossing halfway this chart.... you have to picture a new triangle of resistance forming between those ribbons,..... you now can only see the blue-ish ribbon. The yellow TF5Zone draws the other line on the bottom...... and there is your MultiTimeFrame Triangle where ultimately price is either going to break out to the upside or to the downside.

So let's sum it up: What you see develop here is a dynamic drawn Triangle influenced by all the necessary TF's to make your decision on.....

The stronger resistance is above price. Therefore you already know one thing for sure... Price will come down.

What you don't know yet is where exactly will this happen? This information is provided by the Yellow TF5Zone widening up and simultaneously crossing below the Magenta Zone. Next you see to trials to breakout to the downside.... the last one succeeds: First Price falls through the opening up Red TF1Zone and immediately now price falls down through the opening up Yellow TF5Zone as well. Exactly there you take your short entry..... for all resistance underneath now has been broken.

Cheers, John

--- 帖子 #2166 ---
Good observation. Here there are two possible entries for Long:

1. Right at the bottom of the TF30Zone (Magenta) at the second Blue Dot around 10:15 hrs.... exactly above TF1Zone.

Price stops at narrowing TF15Zone (Blue). Next Price retraces nicely back towards the combo support of TF1Zone and TF30Zone traders.... than again price wants to go up again and now breaks through the TF15Zone

2. The second entry is what I call a Gateway Passage. (BTW Other examples of Gataway passages are in the pdf-file compiled by Jazz1964). Exactly at the red line you have drawn here at 11:17 hrs price passes the crossing of TF15Zone ribbons right in the middle. (= Gateway)

--- 帖子 #2175 ---
Hi Pipster,

Did you try this? It' s in the code.

"   LocalTimeZone: TimeZone for which MT4 shows your local time,

e.g. 1 or 2 for Europe (GMT+1 or GMT+2 (daylight

savings time).  Use zero for no adjustment.

DestTimeZone:  TimeZone for the session from which to calculate

the levels (e.g. 1 or 2 for the European session

(without or with daylight savings time).

Use zero for GMT

Example: If your MT server is living in the EST (Eastern Standard Time,

GMT-5) zone and want to calculate the levels for the London trading

session (European time in summer GMT+1), then enter -5 for

LocalTimeZone, 1 for Dest TimeZone.

Please understand that the LocalTimeZone setting depends on the

time on your MetaTrader charts (for example the demo server

from MetaQuotes always lives in CDT (+2) or CET (+1), no matter

what the clock on your wall says.

If in doubt, leave everything to zero. "

--- 帖子 #2177 ---
Kijun and Tenkan lines are both a kind of moving averages with different settings. We only use one of these lines, The Kijun (29).

The way we use it is for tradeguidance, we look how price is situated to the line. If price is above the line, we don't like entry shorts at that moment and vice versa.

You can also use the Kijun for guiding your exit.

Read the posts on page 135, it is described there.

Or search the pdf file on the word 'KijunTenkan'....

Got it?

--- 帖子 #2192 ---
Hey LSs,

Yes I was aware of the TF30 Ribbon, which could give support. But everything was strong pointing down whith power while TF30 was widening (so not too much Support).

Funny you asked this, because at my entry I thought about your own remark today, saying " .....being too careful sometimes? (: )"

I know there are people scanning all threads about trading systems searching for the holy grail which have to make them rich without investing in time and knowledge. I have never been such a trader (and student). And I know some very good traders have looked to the Ribbon system and didn't take the time to find the big benefits of it.....no prob at all.
I found that the ribbons always give you a very good view on what is happening right now. I have had in the past trading systems on my chart from which I thought "yes this is great" but after a while I always thought: okay, my indicators are giving me a signal right now, but I don't have a good feel where we are and if it is okay to trust the signal...... so I didn't take the trade...and didn't take the next one. But with the ribbons in combination with some good indicators I got a good feel about what is happening, where are the risks and where are the better opportunities.

The ribbons sometimes don't let me trade a nice move, saying me it isn't a high prob trade. Yes, sometimes I feel sad about that. But looking at my trade results I am very proud that I have so less bad trades!! I am sure it is the result of knowing when the risk of sideways markets is there, .....and of getting whipsawed. So I actually don't mind to miss some good trades.

At the other hand, it also happens I enter a trade very early after a reversal, because the ribbons tell me it is okay.

When your friend thinks it is complicated, He is most likely looking to a part of the chart where the ribbons are not matching. When he thinks "what is this??" ....well, don't trade at that point, I think it is not a good trading setup! Good opportunities with Ribbos are looking clear! So when it is not clear, it is not good to trade.

In this thread there is enough material gathered to learn the ribbons in a few days. The pdf will help for sure and in post#1 everything is available to setup the chart. Also you know there are people who will give support.

Cheers, Jazz

1) The indicator display in the main chart window is not very clear when price is drawn over the indicator.

2) another way to print the distances is this:
close below R1:       10   35               }
close below R5:       10   35      }   price is below all ribbons!
close below R15:    10   35          }
close below R30:    10   35          }

close above R1:        10   35               }
close above R5:          10   35 }
close above R15:     10  35          }   price is above all ribbons!
close above R30:  10  35          }

close below R1:   10   35             }

close in R5:                     10  35            }
close above R15:     10   35           }   messy situation!
close below R30:     10   35          }

Such an indicator can replace the #Kino_close_above_ribbons indicator.

Close_above indicator is great for visuality of history, so people can attach it also (when the indi is ready)....in that case the indi I describe here could be displayed at the right side of close_above indi.

--- 帖子 #2215 ---
This chartgraph is currenty clearly in an NTZ. There are two reasons for that:

First of all notice how close the yellow Spudfibo lines are packed together... everyone of those can be a line support or resistance. Longs as well as shorts in such areas bounce to soon on those lines. Preferably pipdistance has to be more than 35 to get into a trade.....

At the end of this chart on the right you can see how difficult it is for price to get above the Spudfibo.... Price falls back to make a retracement towards yellow TF5Zone >>>>> There would be a chance for a breakout to the upside.... However all these Spudfibo's close together still makes it risky to enter a long here. How did it go from there?

Secondly price and TF1Zone are for the greater part in this chart in between TF15 and TF5 Zone. These Zones here also are too close together to enter trades. The better trade setups arrive when TF1Zone makes a retracement back towards TF5Zone (or sometimes TF15Zone) under or above all other Zones.

Furthermore support and resistance is in the TFZones itself in the first place. How to use triangles to determine breakouts, please check some examples I gave on page 132..... F.i. in one example where you can see that the stronger resistance is provided by the lower TFZones (i.e. TF15 and TF30).

Hope this helps, John
